# The Year-End Money Market Storm - Conks
+ author: Conks
+ source: https://www.conks.plumbing/p/the-treasury-market-black-swan?utm_source=publication-search
> a calm year is set for a volatile conclusion

---
_— programming note: it looks like the Fed and I are on the same page. while I was proofreading and publishing this piece, officials [announced](https://www.reuters.com/markets/us/ny-fed-adds-extra-daily-standing-repo-operation-covering-year-end-2024-12-19/) they would offer early repo operations at the SRF to contain money market pressures. let’s see if it helps…_

The buzz around another explosive [year-end](https://www.ecb.europa.eu/press/financial-stability-publications/fsr/focus/2008/pdf/ecb~ae9412ca00.fsrbox200806_08.pdf), the period infamous for banks pulling back from key dollar markets, has once again emerged. Demand for funding has soared this year, [pushing](https://www.newyorkfed.org/markets/counterparties/primary-dealers-statistics) dealer balance sheets to their limits. The Fed’s QT[1](https://www.conks.plumbing/p/the-treasury-market-black-swan?utm_source=publication-search#footnote-1-152574525) continues to [fuel](https://www.financialresearch.gov/hedge-fund-monitor/categories/size/chart-4/) hedge fund demand for [basis trades](https://substack.com/home/post/p-136675602?utm_campaign=post&utm_medium=web)[2](https://www.conks.plumbing/p/the-treasury-market-black-swan?utm_source=publication-search#footnote-2-152574525), while euphoria has prompted increasing amounts of levered stock market exposure. Rates to finance such trades have risen so broadly that [SOFR](https://www.newyorkfed.org/markets/reference-rates/sofr) — the benchmark funding cost — now [trades](https://substackcdn.com/image/fetch/f_auto,q_auto:good,fl_progressive:steep/https%3A%2F%2Fsubstack-post-media.s3.amazonaws.com%2Fpublic%2Fimages%2F3d4eaec9-9320-4a2c-97c3-654a3301c2f2_12314x9158.png) consistently above an undead Fed Funds (FF) rate. Dealers have even been forced to venture into the darkest depths of funding markets to tap riskier yet cheaper dollars, with trading volumes in the most neglected markets — such as asset-backed commercial paper (ABCP) — staging a mini-comeback. The scene is now set for another year-end rate upheaval.

[

![](https://substackcdn.com/image/fetch/$s_!MUy2!,w_1456,c_limit,f_auto,q_auto:good,fl_progressive:steep/https%3A%2F%2Fsubstack-post-media.s3.amazonaws.com%2Fpublic%2Fimages%2F8e71a5dc-82b9-4764-9c3f-154672dc899b_8726x5692.png)

](https://substackcdn.com/image/fetch/$s_!MUy2!,f_auto,q_auto:good,fl_progressive:steep/https%3A%2F%2Fsubstack-post-media.s3.amazonaws.com%2Fpublic%2Fimages%2F8e71a5dc-82b9-4764-9c3f-154672dc899b_8726x5692.png)

The media spotlight, meanwhile, [has](https://www.ft.com/content/dd359460-13c7-4a81-b59d-00bd91e3cbf7) [shone](https://www.bloomberg.com/news/articles/2024-11-14/jpmorgan-sees-surge-in-demand-for-equity-backed-repos-persisting) on another obscure market putting pressure on dealers: equity repo. For the past year, market makers have financed numerous baskets of large-cap stocks to meet the insatiable demand for longs. An intense craving for stock market exposure and a subsequent rise in price has boosted volumes of [equity repos](https://www.newyorkfed.org/data-and-statistics/data-visualization/tri-party-repo#interactive/volume) on the BNY’s (Bank of New York’s) [triparty](https://www.conks.plumbing/p/the-triparty-repo-market) platform. Dealers fund some client positions by purchasing stocks and pledging them for cash in repos[3](https://www.conks.plumbing/p/the-treasury-market-black-swan?utm_source=publication-search#footnote-3-152574525), paying an overnight rate until they no longer need funding. While dealers have met the need for longs from hedge funds and other investors, a plunge in short-selling activity has hindered the securities lending market, where dealers usually earn a spread[4](https://www.conks.plumbing/p/the-treasury-market-black-swan?utm_source=publication-search#footnote-4-152574525) for loaning equities from their inventories to short sellers. Instead, massive demand for not just longs but leveraged longs has forced market makers to charge a colossal fee, sometimes 100bps (1.00%) or more above SOFR, to warehouse[5](https://www.conks.plumbing/p/the-treasury-market-black-swan?utm_source=publication-search#footnote-5-152574525) equities on their already crowded balance sheets.

[

![](https://substackcdn.com/image/fetch/$s_!gD5r!,w_1456,c_limit,f_auto,q_auto:good,fl_progressive:steep/https%3A%2F%2Fsubstack-post-media.s3.amazonaws.com%2Fpublic%2Fimages%2Fb695a29a-2470-4229-ad51-4403a0bd5cc9_8840x5692.png)

](https://substackcdn.com/image/fetch/$s_!gD5r!,f_auto,q_auto:good,fl_progressive:steep/https%3A%2F%2Fsubstack-post-media.s3.amazonaws.com%2Fpublic%2Fimages%2Fb695a29a-2470-4229-ad51-4403a0bd5cc9_8840x5692.png)

Simultaneously, a mammoth increase in issuance and an undesirable yield curve have reduced demand for U.S. sovereign debt. Unlike equities, the Fed’s primary dealers serve as the private sovereign debt buyers of last resort and must absorb the largest amount of unwelcome inventory on record. In the [secured standard](https://www.conks.plumbing/p/the-rise-of-the-secured-standard), providing room on your balance sheet is already costly. But now, the supply-demand imbalance in multiple markets has caused the scarcity of funding to reach precarious levels, just as we approach the most restrictive period on the financial calendar. A stormy year-end is looming.

The cost of obtaining leveraged exposure to large-cap stocks has ballooned, not only in the U.S. but worldwide. Across all durations, lending rates have increased in line with positioning, which has grown uncomfortably [bullish](https://www.ft.com/__origami/service/image/v2/images/raw/ftcms%3A98504d66-ad11-4a41-b618-23c5c0aadc01?source=next-article&fit=scale-down&quality=highest&width=700&dpr=1). The upside of higher funding costs has been a cheapening in put option hedges for those aiming to protect their equity gains. Meanwhile, those looking to “get in and stay in” via leverage must pay a hefty premium.

These leveraged equity positions provided by dealers to hedge funds have somehow gained the title of “equity repo”, confusing many fixed-income traders. Hedge funds do not use repos but obtain leverage supplied by dealers — who might use a repo to finance hedge fund trades. If we play along anyway, equity repos in triparty have been funding “equity repos,” where the latter is a leveraged trade that hedge funds enter through various instruments. Total return swaps (TRS), for instance, have become a popular vehicle. Market makers finance a basket of equities (sometimes via repo) and then lease them to investors, who receive cash flows equal to the “total return” — i.e. dividends plus price appreciation. The dealer has technically entered a long and short position while charging the hedge fund a spread for liquidity.

In an example funding chain, the dealer buys an equity basket and funds the purchase using a repo negotiated with a cash lender. The dealer pledges these assets from its custodial account at the [DTC](https://www.dtcc.com/about/businesses-and-subsidiaries/dtc) (Depository Trust Company), “the guardian of U.S. equities”, boosting the cash balance in its clearing account[6](https://www.conks.plumbing/p/the-treasury-market-black-swan?utm_source=publication-search#footnote-6-152574525). At the same time, the cash lender knows it will earn a secure return and can sell the equity collateral to make itself whole if the dealer defaults. Cash and equities are thus “locked up” on the BNY’s platform, with both parties knowing they don’t need to trade or transfer the assets before the repo unwinds.

An hour or so later, the dealer and an institutional investor enter into a total return swap. The dealer passes on the costs of warehousing the basket of equities on its books, charging SOFR + 100bps. Until clients exit their positions, dealers roll their triparty repos (or other funding sources) at lower rates, earning a juicy market-making spread. Dealers also offer clients long exposures via other mechanisms, such as futures — by hedging a short futures position with a funded basket of equities. The increasing range of equity products, such as leveraged ETFs and other emerging assets, has likely added further strains on market makers.

The era of congested balance sheets will likely persist until the Fed ceases QT and the yield curve[7](https://www.conks.plumbing/p/the-treasury-market-black-swan?utm_source=publication-search#footnote-7-152574525) steepens further. As for equity markets, a prolonged selloff will provide some relief. Stock market unrest will divert cash previously used to fund equity longs, for which demand is no longer present, toward money markets. As positive carry turns into negative carry in equities, dealer desks within the same bank entity — sometimes on the same trading floor — will play funding “hot potato”. An overfunded equity desk will arm their neighboring swap desks with excess cash to fund FX swap trades, driving a tightening[8](https://www.conks.plumbing/p/the-treasury-market-black-swan?utm_source=publication-search#footnote-8-152574525) of cross-currency (XCCY) bases while easing pressure on “equity repo” rates.

[

![](https://substackcdn.com/image/fetch/$s_!nmhX!,w_1456,c_limit,f_auto,q_auto:good,fl_progressive:steep/https%3A%2F%2Fsubstack-post-media.s3.amazonaws.com%2Fpublic%2Fimages%2Fb22dcd17-a9cf-4be2-a3e1-5987b9c54af1_8956x5692.png)

](https://substackcdn.com/image/fetch/$s_!nmhX!,f_auto,q_auto:good,fl_progressive:steep/https%3A%2F%2Fsubstack-post-media.s3.amazonaws.com%2Fpublic%2Fimages%2Fb22dcd17-a9cf-4be2-a3e1-5987b9c54af1_8956x5692.png)

an increasingly negative number means dollar funding demand exceeds supply

But if the usual bullish [seasonality](https://x.com/Geiger_Capital/status/1867654436832657770) emerges during late December, a Santa rally will ensure spreads widen and funding costs remain elevated. Scarce liquidity from banks engaging in window dressing _(as illustrated below)_ will produce rate spikes at year-end that most money market participants will not soon forget. Traders on short-term desks have thus begun to lock in[9](https://www.conks.plumbing/p/the-treasury-market-black-swan?utm_source=publication-search#footnote-9-152574525) funding over the bumpiest parts of year-end, so-called turn trades, which have already traded at a premium to earlier episodes.

[

![](https://substackcdn.com/image/fetch/$s_!saFs!,w_1456,c_limit,f_auto,q_auto:good,fl_progressive:steep/https%3A%2F%2Fsubstack-post-media.s3.amazonaws.com%2Fpublic%2Fimages%2Fe6f8910b-115b-4ae0-a3e3-3b58154f2be8_6178x8210.png)

](https://substackcdn.com/image/fetch/$s_!saFs!,f_auto,q_auto:good,fl_progressive:steep/https%3A%2F%2Fsubstack-post-media.s3.amazonaws.com%2Fpublic%2Fimages%2Fe6f8910b-115b-4ae0-a3e3-3b58154f2be8_6178x8210.png)

click to enlarge (best viewed on desktop - [light mode](https://www.conks.plumbing/p/infographics-bank-window-dressing))

Some relief will arrive in the form of reserves flowing into the banking system from the TGA, the U.S. government’s bank account, as the debt ceiling deadline looms large. Moreover, the ~$130 billion [lingering](https://fred.stlouisfed.org/series/RRPONTSYD) in the Fed’s RRP could also be tapped by money funds with more counterparties to lend to via the [expansion](https://www.dtcc.com/charts/membership) of central clearing. An additional [5 basis point cut](https://www.treasuryandrisk.com/2024/12/18/fed-lowers-interest-rates-by-a-quarter-point/#:~:text=The%20Fed%20also%20announced%20it%20would%20reduce%20the%20rate%20it%20pays%20lenders%20using%20its%20overnight%20reverse%20repurchase%20(RRP)%20facility%20by%2030%20basis%20points%20(bps).) to the Fed’s RRP rate, implemented at the latest FOMC meeting, will also relieve tensions, alongside early SRF operations ([just announced](https://www.reuters.com/markets/us/ny-fed-adds-extra-daily-standing-repo-operation-covering-year-end-2024-12-19/)) to contain money market pressures.

Even so, these enhancements will be no match for the mixture of year-end catalysts about to impede money markets. On top of constrained balance sheets, numerous year-end pressures will soon materialize. Money funds, abandoned by their usual dealer and bank counterparties, will be forced to park surplus cash in the Fed’s RRP, a [reserve-draining](https://www.conks.plumbing/p/infographics-the-mechanics-of-the) facility. Those same banks, having seen their stock prices rise dramatically, will shrink their repo and derivatives exposures further to sidestep higher [G-SIB surcharges](https://www.bis.org/bcbs/gsib/index.htm), which forces banks to hold more equity as their risk profile expands. What’s more, unlike last year, dealers must help facilitate $120 billion in U.S. Treasury settlements, a higher dose than September’s mini [upheaval](https://www.reuters.com/markets/us/fed-liquidity-tools-see-demand-ease-amid-new-repo-market-anxieties-2024-10-01/). With Basel III and Dodd-Frank also in full swing, the flow of liquidity has grown more warped than ever. JPMorgan, the private lender of last resort, will soon find its hoard of reserves inadequate to bridge all imbalances without help from the central bank’s balance sheet. As demand for a [global dollar backstop](https://www.conks.plumbing/p/infographics-the-federal-reserves) rises[10](https://www.conks.plumbing/p/the-treasury-market-black-swan?utm_source=publication-search#footnote-10-152574525), the Fed’s [swap line network](https://www.conks.plumbing/p/infographics-the-plumbing-of-global) will briefly jump into overdrive. Still, this won’t prevent a funding squeeze from pushing short-term rates above the Fed’s target range. Fasten your seatbelts and brace for a stormy year-end rate spike.

_**If you enjoyed this, hit the ♡ button below the footnotes to let us know (it helps us grow) and share a link/message on social media. Comments are also encouraged. Thanks for being a Conks Subscriber!**_

# The Great Rebalancing - Conks
+ author: Conks
+ source: https://www.conks.plumbing/p/the-treasury-market-black-swan?utm_source=publication-search
> the war on long-end bond issuance is just beginning

---
After vowing to disrupt the “nothing ever happens” era established by the previous administration, the latest band of U.S. leaders has again reverted to prioritizing the stability of the UST (U.S. Treasury) market over political objectives. The Treasury Sec. has pivoted from slamming predecessors to not only embracing but enhancing the strategy of postponing duration issuance, reducing (some) tension at the long end of the curve. Increased [Treasury buybacks](https://treasurydirect.gov/auctions/announcements-data-results/buy-backs/), aimed at strengthening the darkest regions of the U.S. sovereign bond market, should arrive momentarily, followed by the case for delaying an increase in coupon (i.e. note and bond) issuance by a few more _years_, not quarters.

[

![](https://substackcdn.com/image/fetch/$s_!lAIX!,w_1456,c_limit,f_auto,q_auto:good,fl_progressive:steep/https%3A%2F%2Fsubstack-post-media.s3.amazonaws.com%2Fpublic%2Fimages%2Febef692f-5935-41e5-903c-d5117258ea33_5294x2750.png)

](https://substackcdn.com/image/fetch/$s_!lAIX!,f_auto,q_auto:good,fl_progressive:steep/https%3A%2F%2Fsubstack-post-media.s3.amazonaws.com%2Fpublic%2Fimages%2Febef692f-5935-41e5-903c-d5117258ea33_5294x2750.png)

click to enlarge (best viewed on desktop)

Luckily for the U.S. empire, global finance remains hungry for ultra-short-term U.S. debt. Stablecoin issuers and money funds can’t live without it, while foreign buyers can’t get enough, earning a substantial premium over dollar deposits. The U.S. central bank’s asset portfolio, the [SOMA](https://www.newyorkfed.org/markets/soma-holdings) (System Open Market Account), has grown ravenous too. Officials will thus soon need to uphold the Fed’s [ample reserve regime](https://www.federalreserve.gov/econres/notes/feds-notes/implementing-monetary-policy-in-an-ample-reserves-regime-the-basics-note-1-of-3-20200701.html), staving off a repeat of the [repocalypse](https://www.conks.plumbing/p/the-feds-repo-defensive-part-one?utm_source=publication-search) by resuming UST purchases[1](https://www.conks.plumbing/p/the-treasury-market-black-swan?utm_source=publication-search#footnote-1-168494743) as early as the end of this year. Despite potentially [crowding out](https://www.omfif.org/2024/12/the-fed-should-stay-out-of-the-fight-for-t-bills/) supply and [disrupting](https://www.omfif.org/2024/12/the-fed-should-stay-out-of-the-fight-for-t-bills/) cash-futures basis trades, most Fed alchemists desire to match the duration of the SOMA to the outstanding UST market. Post the conclusion of QT (quantitative tightening), the “Fed’s portfolio managers” are likely set to feast on — and reinvest MBS proceeds[2](https://www.conks.plumbing/p/the-treasury-market-black-swan?utm_source=publication-search#footnote-2-168494743) into — bills.

[

![](https://substackcdn.com/image/fetch/$s_!mwhM!,w_1456,c_limit,f_auto,q_auto:good,fl_progressive:steep/https%3A%2F%2Fsubstack-post-media.s3.amazonaws.com%2Fpublic%2Fimages%2F64075b53-5d99-4c19-aa46-09b1e3530d2d_6147x5924.png)

](https://substackcdn.com/image/fetch/$s_!mwhM!,f_auto,q_auto:good,fl_progressive:steep/https%3A%2F%2Fsubstack-post-media.s3.amazonaws.com%2Fpublic%2Fimages%2F64075b53-5d99-4c19-aa46-09b1e3530d2d_6147x5924.png)

U.S. central bank OMOs in action…

Alongside its existing OMOs (open market operations), such as o/n (overnight) repos at the [SRF](https://www.newyorkfed.org/markets/repo-agreement-ops-faq), the Fed’s RMOs (reserve management operations) will vacuum up ultra-short-term issuance, initiating both a significant SOMA rebalancing and a quiet demolition of interest rate risk previously absorbed during various crises. Presently, bank reserves continue to deplete via QT, as Fed RRPs — the unwinding of which releases reserves back into the banking system — hover around zero. This is ensuing just as the average maturity in the Fed’s portfolio has increased, setting the stage for Operation Untwist, the near-reverse mechanism of Operation Twist[3](https://www.conks.plumbing/p/the-treasury-market-black-swan?utm_source=publication-search#footnote-3-168494743) that produced a bill drought in the SOMA. A return to a “neutral” Fed portfolio is subsequently looming.

With no immediate downside to consider, the Fed will proceed with unveiling its plan to not only shorten the WAM (weighted-average maturity i.e. the average bond maturity) of its portfolio but do so as swiftly as possible. “Swiftly” in Fed speak implies five years at the least and two decades at the most, with the second timescale proving undesirable. Monetary leaders will therefore choose the speediest course of action. RMOs will likely reach $20-25 billion in bills purchased per month, while Treasury notes and bonds that mature will be replaced with ultra-short-term sovereign debt. MBS (mortgage-backed securities) cash proceeds could also be reinvested (into bills) to quicken the rebalancing.

Meanwhile, the U.S. Treasury is executing its own parallel rebalance. Worries around “t-bill abuse” have arisen, but officials have ample room to use America’s exorbitant privilege[4](https://www.conks.plumbing/p/the-treasury-market-black-swan?utm_source=publication-search#footnote-4-168494743) and expand bill supply. Concerns that the U.S. Treasury could accumulate too much rollover risk by issuing excessive short-term debt are presently overblown. Most UST redemptions involve t-bills already covered by the Treasury’s self-imposed buffer equal to five days of cash outflows from the Treasury General Account (TGA)[5](https://www.conks.plumbing/p/the-treasury-market-black-swan?utm_source=publication-search#footnote-5-168494743), a cushion specifically designed to offset any technically induced shortfalls. Shortening the WAM of outstanding Treasury debt so that up to 25% consists of bills will barely raise the threat level on an already nonexistent hazard. Thus, with the U.S. central bank’s forthcoming rebalancing expected to proceed without much backlash, the Treasury will soon have another guaranteed buyer of bills at the most opportune moment. The two American monetary juggernauts are now destined to press their advantage.

[

![](https://substackcdn.com/image/fetch/$s_!V0dJ!,w_1456,c_limit,f_auto,q_auto:good,fl_progressive:steep/https%3A%2F%2Fsubstack-post-media.s3.amazonaws.com%2Fpublic%2Fimages%2Fea1cf74f-3ab2-4d74-a716-78799a89d155_1919x1270.png)

](https://substackcdn.com/image/fetch/$s_!V0dJ!,f_auto,q_auto:good,fl_progressive:steep/https%3A%2F%2Fsubstack-post-media.s3.amazonaws.com%2Fpublic%2Fimages%2Fea1cf74f-3ab2-4d74-a716-78799a89d155_1919x1270.png)

still much more room for short-term issuance…

These two rebalancings will gain the swift backing of both the Treasury Sec and POTUS, who in classic $-hegemonic style have again u-turned from trying to curb the deficit. Uncoincidentally, President Trump has also joined Bessent’s initiative to avoid adding extra duration to the market[6](https://www.conks.plumbing/p/the-treasury-market-black-swan?utm_source=publication-search#footnote-6-168494743) — issuance that the Fed will soon wish to avoid absorbing. Similar ideas have spread worldwide, resulting in a globally synchronized war on long-end issuance and volatility. Japan’s MoF (Ministry of Finance) has [announced](https://www.bloomberg.com/news/articles/2025-06-20/japan-set-to-cut-super-long-bond-issuance-by-more-than-expected) plans to reduce long-term JGB (Japanese government bond) issuance, while it is rumored to consider buying back the same “super-long” debt. In the UK, the Bank of England (BoE) responded to Trump’s tariff cascade by delaying long-end gilt auctions in favor of the short-end. BoE Governor Bailey also [hinted](https://www.bloomberg.com/news/articles/2025-07-01/boe-governor-bailey-hints-at-slowing-pace-of-qt-bond-sales) at ending QT early due to a “global steepening” of yield curves.

Relying on turning the bill printer up to the max, however, won’t work forever, even for the mighty USA. Once you approach an unhealthy share of bills[7](https://www.conks.plumbing/p/the-treasury-market-black-swan?utm_source=publication-search#footnote-7-168494743), the market starts to second-guess your Treasury’s doctrine of “regular and predictable issuance”, enforced initially to _avoid_ spooking the market. Doing so means paying the penalty of investors demanding higher rates at longer, more vulnerable parts of the curve. Nevertheless, despite leaders acknowledging their debt piles have grown to unsustainable levels and some questioning a heavy bill strategy, the same approaches have been in place for decades. Monetary leaders can and will continue to maintain the status quo, unless the consequences become evident. The fight to rein in the long-end via supply maneuvers will persist until the regular and predictable becomes the irregular and uncertain. By then, more “extraordinary measures” will need to be implemented.
